      <p><b>Guyana</b> (pronounced <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AH_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AH-9">[9]</a></sup> officially the <b>Co‑operative Republic of Guyana</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-ISW_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISW-10">[10]</a></sup> is a country on the northern mainland of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and the capital city is Georgetown. It is part of the mainland <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean region</a> maintaining its strong cultural, historical, and political ties with other <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> countries and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM). Guyana is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> to the south and southwest, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> to the west, and <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> to the east. With 215,000 square kilometres (83,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), Guyana is the third-smallest <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> by area in mainland South America after <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>; it is also the <a href="/wiki/List_of_South_American_countries_by_population" title="List of South American countries by population">second-least populous sovereign state in South America</a> after Suriname. </p>
      <p>The region known as "<a href="/wiki/The_Guianas" title="The Guianas">the Guianas</a>" consists of the <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Shield" title="Guiana Shield">large shield landmass</a> north of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a> and east of the <a href="/wiki/Orinoco" title="Orinoco">Orinoco River</a> known as the "land of many waters". There are nine <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Guyana" title="Indigenous peoples in Guyana">indigenous</a> tribes residing in Guyana: the <a href="/wiki/Wai-wai_people" title="Wai-wai people">Wai Wai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macushi_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Macushi people">Macushi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patamona_people" title="Patamona people">Patamona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lokono" title="Lokono">Lokono</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalina_people" title="Kalina people">Kalina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wapishana_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Wapishana people">Wapishana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pemon_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pemon people">Pemon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akawaio_people" title="Akawaio people">Akawaio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warao_people" title="Warao people">Warao</a>. Historically dominated by the Lokono and Kalina tribes, Guyana was colonised by the Dutch before coming under <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British control</a> in the late 18th century. It was governed as <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">British Guiana</a>, with a mostly plantation-style economy until the 1950s. It gained independence in 1966, and officially became a republic within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> in 1970. The legacy of British rule is reflected in the country's political administration and diverse population, which includes <a href="/wiki/Indo-Guyanese" title="Indo-Guyanese">Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afro-Guyanese" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Guyanese">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Guyana" title="Indigenous peoples in Guyana">Amerindian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Guyanese" title="Chinese Guyanese">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guyanese" title="Portuguese Guyanese">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_Caribbeans" title="White Caribbeans">other European</a>, and various multiracial groups. In 2017, 41% of the population of Guyana lived below the <a href="/wiki/Poverty_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Poverty line">poverty line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Guyana is the only South American nation in which English is the official language. The majority of the population, however, speak <a href="/wiki/Guyanese_Creole" title="Guyanese Creole">Guyanese Creole</a>, an <a href="/wiki/English-based_creole_language" class="mw-redirect" title="English-based creole language">English-based creole language</a>, as a first language. Guyana is part of the <a href="/wiki/Anglophone_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglophone Caribbean">Anglophone Caribbean</a>. CARICOM <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_(administrative_office)" title="Secretariat (administrative office)">headquarters</a> is in Guyana's capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Guyana" title="Georgetown, Guyana">Georgetown</a>. In 2008, the country joined the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a> as a founding member. </p>

        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Government_and_politics"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Government and politics</span></a>

          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Electricity"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Electricity</span></a></li> 
         </ul> </li> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name "Guyana" derives from <i>Guiana</i>, the original name for the region that formerly included Guyana (British Guiana), Suriname (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_colonization_of_the_Guianas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch colonization of the Guianas">Dutch Guiana</a>), French Guiana, and parts of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, Venezuela and Brazil. According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i>, "Guyana" comes from an indigenous Amerindian language and means "land of many waters".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Guyana" title="History of Guyana">History of Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:LocationNetherlandsGuiana.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/LocationNetherlandsGuiana.png/220px-LocationNetherlandsGuiana.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="101" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/01/LocationNetherlandsGuiana.png 1.5x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="115"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:LocationNetherlandsGuiana.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Dutch Guiana 1667–1814
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are nine <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Guyana" title="Indigenous peoples in Guyana">indigenous</a> tribes residing in Guyana: the <a href="/wiki/Wai-wai_people" title="Wai-wai people">Wai Wai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macushi_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Macushi people">Macushi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patamona_people" title="Patamona people">Patamona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lokono" title="Lokono">Lokono</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalina_people" title="Kalina people">Kalina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wapishana_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Wapishana people">Wapishana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pemon_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pemon people">Pemon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akawaio_people" title="Akawaio people">Akawaio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warao_people" title="Warao people">Warao</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Historically, the Lokono and Kalina tribes dominated Guyana. Although <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> was the first European to sight Guyana during his third voyage (in 1498), and Sir <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">Walter Raleigh</a> wrote an account in 1596, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch</a> were the first Europeans to establish colonies: <a href="/wiki/Pomeroon_(colony)" title="Pomeroon (colony)">Pomeroon</a> (1581), <a href="/wiki/Essequibo_(colony)" title="Essequibo (colony)">Essequibo</a> (1616), <a href="/wiki/Berbice" title="Berbice">Berbice</a> (1627), and <a href="/wiki/Demerara" title="Demerara">Demerara</a> (1752). After the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">British</a> assumed control in 1796,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> the Dutch formally ceded the area in 1814. In 1831 the three separate colonies became a single British colony known as <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">British Guiana</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Boundary_lines_of_British_Guiana_1896.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Boundary_lines_of_British_Guiana_1896.jpg/220px-Boundary_lines_of_British_Guiana_1896.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Boundary_lines_of_British_Guiana_1896.jpg/330px-Boundary_lines_of_British_Guiana_1896.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Boundary_lines_of_British_Guiana_1896.jpg/440px-Boundary_lines_of_British_Guiana_1896.jpg 2x" data-file-width="925" data-file-height="1388"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Boundary_lines_of_British_Guiana_1896.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">British Guiana</a> from 1896
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since its independence in 1824, Venezuela has claimed the area of land to the west of the <a href="/wiki/Essequibo_River" title="Essequibo River">Essequibo River</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a> wrote to the British government warning against the Berbice and Demerara settlers settling on land which the Venezuelans, as assumed heirs of Spanish claims on the area dating to the sixteenth century, claimed was theirs. In 1899 an international tribunal ruled the land belonged to Great Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The British territorial claim stemmed from Dutch involvement and colonization of the area also dating to the sixteenth century, which was ceded to the British. </p>
      <p>Guyana achieved independence from the United Kingdom as a dominion on 26 May 1966 and became a republic on 23 February 1970, remaining a member of the Commonwealth. Shortly after independence, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> began to take diplomatic, economic and military action against Guyana in order to enforce its territorial claim to the <a href="/wiki/Guayana_Esequiba" title="Guayana Esequiba">Guayana Esequiba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:56_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:56-17">[17]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">US State Department</a> and the US <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> (CIA), along with the British government, also played a strong role in influencing political control in Guyana during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The American government supported <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Burnham" title="Forbes Burnham">Forbes Burnham</a> during the early years of independence because <a href="/wiki/Cheddi_Jagan" title="Cheddi Jagan">Cheddi Jagan</a> was identified as a <a href="/wiki/Marxist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist">Marxist</a>. They provided secret financial support and political campaign advice to Burnham's <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Congress_(Guyana)" title="People's National Congress (Guyana)">People's National Congress</a>, to the detriment of the Jagan-led <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Progressive_Party_(Guyana)" title="People's Progressive Party (Guyana)">People's Progressive Party</a>, which was mostly supported by Guyanese of East Indian background. </p>
      <p>In 1974, the Guyana government leased 1,500 hectares (3,800 acres) of land to <a href="/wiki/Peoples_Temple" title="Peoples Temple">Peoples Temple</a>, an American new religious movement, led by pastor <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jones" title="Jim Jones">Jim Jones</a>. The settlement, informally called "<a href="/wiki/Jonestown" title="Jonestown">Jonestown</a>", eventually grew to a population of about 1,000 people, mostly emigrated from the United States. In 1978, Guyana received worldwide attention when 909 people died in a mass murder/suicide in Jonestown by drinking cyanide-laced <a href="/wiki/Flavor_Aid" title="Flavor Aid">Flavor Aid</a>. A day prior, U.S. congressman <a href="/wiki/Leo_Ryan" title="Leo Ryan">Leo Ryan</a> had visited and toured the settlement as part of an investigation. As he was preparing to leave at the <a href="/wiki/Port_Kaituma" title="Port Kaituma">Port Kaituma</a> airstrip, a group of Peoples Temple members pulled up and opened fire on the visiting delegation, killing Ryan and four other people. </p>
      <p>In May 2008, President <a href="/wiki/Bharrat_Jagdeo" title="Bharrat Jagdeo">Bharrat Jagdeo</a> was a signatory to the <a href="/wiki/UNASUR_Constitutive_Treaty" title="UNASUR Constitutive Treaty">UNASUR Constitutive Treaty</a> of the Union of South American Nations. The Guyanese government officially ratified the treaty in 2010. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Guyana" title="Geography of Guyana">Geography of Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GuyanaKaieteurFalls2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/GuyanaKaieteurFalls2004.jpg/170px-GuyanaKaieteurFalls2004.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/GuyanaKaieteurFalls2004.jpg/255px-GuyanaKaieteurFalls2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/GuyanaKaieteurFalls2004.jpg/340px-GuyanaKaieteurFalls2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1439" data-file-height="1531"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GuyanaKaieteurFalls2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kaieteur_Falls" title="Kaieteur Falls">Kaieteur Falls</a> is the world's largest single-drop waterfall by volume.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rupununi_Savannah.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Rupununi_Savannah.jpg/220px-Rupununi_Savannah.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Rupununi_Savannah.jpg/330px-Rupununi_Savannah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Rupununi_Savannah.jpg/440px-Rupununi_Savannah.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rupununi_Savannah.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Rupununi_Savannah" class="mw-redirect" title="Rupununi Savannah">Rupununi Savannah</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The territory controlled by Guyana lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/1st_parallel_north" title="1st parallel north">1°</a> and <a href="/wiki/9th_parallel_north" title="9th parallel north">9°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/56th_meridian_west" title="56th meridian west">56°</a> and <a href="/wiki/62nd_meridian_west" title="62nd meridian west">62°W</a>, and is one of the world's most sparsely populated countries. </p>
      <p>The country can be divided into five natural regions; a narrow and fertile marshy plain along the Atlantic coast (low coastal plain) where most of the population lives; a white sand belt more inland (hilly sand and clay region), containing most of Guyana's mineral deposits; the dense <a href="/wiki/Rain_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Rain forest">rain forests</a> (Forested Highland Region) in the southern part of the country; the drier <a href="/wiki/Savannah" class="mw-redirect" title="Savannah">savannah</a> areas in the south-west; and the smallest interior lowlands (interior savannah) consisting mostly of mountains that gradually rise to the Brazilian border. </p>
      <p>Some of Guyana's highest mountains are <a href="/wiki/Mount_Ayanganna" title="Mount Ayanganna">Mount Ayanganna</a> (2,042 metres or 6,699 feet), <a href="/wiki/Monte_Cabura%C3%AD" title="Monte Caburaí">Monte Caburaí</a> (1,465 metres or 4,806 feet) and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Roraima" title="Mount Roraima">Mount Roraima</a> (2,772 metres or 9,094 feet – the highest mountain in Guyana) on the Brazil-Guyana-Venezuela <a href="/wiki/Tripoint" title="Tripoint">tripoint</a> border, part of the <a href="/wiki/Pakaraima" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakaraima">Pakaraima</a> range. Mount Roraima and Guyana's table-top mountains (<a href="/wiki/Tepui" title="Tepui">tepuis</a>) are said to have been the inspiration for <a href="/wiki/Sir_Arthur_Conan_Doyle" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Arthur Conan Doyle">Sir Arthur Conan Doyle</a>'s 1912 novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lost_World_(Arthur_Conan_Doyle)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lost World (Arthur Conan Doyle)">The Lost World</a></i>. There are also many volcanic <a href="/wiki/Escarpment" title="Escarpment">escarpments</a> and waterfalls, including <a href="/wiki/Kaieteur_Falls" title="Kaieteur Falls">Kaieteur Falls</a> which is believed to be the largest single-drop waterfall in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-independent_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent-19">[19]</a></sup> North of the <a href="/wiki/Rupununi_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Rupununi River">Rupununi River</a> lies the <a href="/wiki/Rupununi_savannah" title="Rupununi savannah">Rupununi savannah</a>, south of which lie the <a href="/wiki/Kanuku_Mountains" title="Kanuku Mountains">Kanuku Mountains</a>. </p>
      <p>The four longest rivers are the Essequibo at 1,010 kilometres (628&nbsp;mi) long, the <a href="/wiki/Courentyne_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Courentyne River">Courentyne River</a> at 724 kilometres (450&nbsp;mi), the <a href="/wiki/Berbice_River" title="Berbice River">Berbice</a> at 595 kilometres (370&nbsp;mi), and the <a href="/wiki/Demerara_River" title="Demerara River">Demerara</a> at 346 kilometres (215&nbsp;mi). The Courentyne river forms the border with Suriname. At the mouth of the Essequibo are several large islands, including the 145&nbsp;km (90&nbsp;mi) wide <a href="/wiki/Shell_Beach,_Guyana" title="Shell Beach, Guyana">Shell Beach</a> along the northwest coast, which is also a major breeding area for <a href="/wiki/Sea_turtle" title="Sea turtle">sea turtles</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/Leatherback_sea_turtle" title="Leatherback sea turtle">leatherbacks</a>) and other wildlife. </p>
      <p>The local climate is <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a> and generally hot and humid, though moderated by northeast <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a> along the coast. There are two rainy seasons, the first from May to mid-August, the second from mid-November to mid-January. </p>
      <p>Guyana has one of the largest unspoiled <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforests</a> in South America, some parts of which are almost inaccessible by humans. The rich natural history of Guyana was described by early explorers <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">Sir Walter Raleigh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Waterton" title="Charles Waterton">Charles Waterton</a> and later by naturalists Sir <a href="/wiki/David_Attenborough" title="David Attenborough">David Attenborough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Durrell" title="Gerald Durrell">Gerald Durrell</a>. In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> broadcast a three-part programme called <i>Lost Land of the Jaguar</i> which highlighted the huge diversity of wildlife, including undiscovered species and rare species such as the <a href="/wiki/Giant_otter" title="Giant otter">giant otter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harpy_eagle" title="Harpy eagle">harpy eagle</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2012, Guyana received a $45 million reward from Norway for its rainforest protection efforts. This stems from a 2009 agreement between the nations for a total of $250 million for protecting and maintaining the natural habitat. Thus far, the country has received $115 million of the total grant. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions_and_Neighbourhood_Councils">Regions and Neighbourhood Councils</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Regions and Neighbourhood Councils">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      </div>

      <p>The regions are divided into 27 neighbourhood councils.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boundary_disputes">Boundary disputes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Boundary disputes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Essequiborivermap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Essequiborivermap.png/250px-Essequiborivermap.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Essequiborivermap.png/375px-Essequiborivermap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Essequiborivermap.png/500px-Essequiborivermap.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Essequiborivermap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Guyana, showing the <a href="/wiki/Essequibo_River" title="Essequibo River">Essequibo River</a> and (shaded dark) the river's drainage basin. Venezuela claims territory up to the western bank of the river. The historical claim by the UK included the river basin well into current-day Venezuela.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Schomburgk_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Schomburgk Line">Schomburgk Line</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_Suriname" title="Borders of Suriname">Borders of Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Guyana is in <a href="/wiki/Territorial_dispute" title="Territorial dispute">border disputes</a> with both Suriname, which claims the area east of the left bank of the <a href="/wiki/Corentyne_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Corentyne River">Corentyne River</a> and the New River in southwestern Suriname, and Venezuela which claims the land west of the Essequibo River, once the <a href="/wiki/Essequibo_(colony)" title="Essequibo (colony)">Dutch colony of Essequibo</a> as part of Venezuela's <a href="/wiki/Guayana_Essequiba" class="mw-redirect" title="Guayana Essequiba">Guayana Essequiba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-foxlatino_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxlatino-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The maritime<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> component of the territorial dispute with Suriname was arbitrated by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Convention_on_Law_of_the_Sea" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Convention on Law of the Sea">United Nations Convention on Law of the Sea</a>, and a ruling was announced on 21 September 2007. The ruling concerning the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> north of both nations found both parties violated treaty obligations and declined to order any compensation to either party.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>When the British surveyed British Guiana in 1840, they included the entire <a href="/wiki/Cuyuni_River" title="Cuyuni River">Cuyuni River</a> basin within the colony. Venezuela did not agree with this as it claimed all lands west of the Essequibo River. In 1898, at Venezuela's request, an international <a href="/wiki/Arbitral_tribunal" title="Arbitral tribunal">arbitration tribunal</a> was convened, and in 1899 the tribunal issued an award giving about 94% of the disputed territory to British Guiana. The arbitration was concluded, settled and accepted into International law by both Venezuela and the U.K. Venezuela brought up again the settled claim, during the 1960s cold war period, and during Guyana's Independence period. This issue is now governed by the Treaty of Geneva of 1966, which was signed by the Governments of Guyana, Great Britain and Venezuela, and Venezuela continues to claim <a href="/wiki/Guayana_Esequiba_(Zona_en_Reclamaci%C3%B3n)" class="mw-redirect" title="Guayana Esequiba (Zona en Reclamación)">Guayana Esequiba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ishmael_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ishmael-30">[30]</a></sup> Venezuela calls this region "Zona en Reclamación" (Reclamation Zone) and Venezuelan maps of the national territory routinely include it, drawing it in with dashed lines.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Specific small disputed areas involving Guyana are <a href="/wiki/Ankoko_Island" title="Ankoko Island">Ankoko Island</a> with Venezuela; Corentyne River<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> with Suriname; and <a href="/wiki/Tigri_Area" title="Tigri Area">Tigri Area</a> or <a href="/wiki/New_River_Triangle" class="mw-redirect" title="New River Triangle">New River Triangle</a><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> with Suriname. In 1967 a Surinamese survey team was found in the New River Triangle and was forcibly removed. In August 1969 a patrol of the <a href="/wiki/Guyana_Defence_Force" title="Guyana Defence Force">Guyana Defence Force</a> found a survey camp and a partially completed airstrip inside the triangle, and documented evidence of the Surinamese intention to occupy the entire disputed area. After an exchange of gunfire, the <a href="/wiki/Surinamese_people" title="Surinamese people">Surinamese</a> were driven from the triangle. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment_and_biodiversity">Environment and biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Environment and biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Flora_of_Guyana" title="Category:Flora of Guyana">Category:Flora of Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Fauna_of_Guyana" title="Category:Fauna of Guyana">Category:Fauna of Guyana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Category:Orchids_of_Guyana" title="Category:Orchids of Guyana">Category:Orchids of Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Guyana_BMNG.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Guyana_BMNG.png/170px-Guyana_BMNG.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Guyana_BMNG.png/255px-Guyana_BMNG.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Guyana_BMNG.png/340px-Guyana_BMNG.png 2x" data-file-width="1294" data-file-height="1910"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Guyana_BMNG.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Satellite image of Guyana from 2004
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Golden_frog_Kaieteur_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Golden_frog_Kaieteur_%282%29.jpg/220px-Golden_frog_Kaieteur_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Golden_frog_Kaieteur_%282%29.jpg/330px-Golden_frog_Kaieteur_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Golden_frog_Kaieteur_%282%29.jpg/440px-Golden_frog_Kaieteur_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1056" data-file-height="749"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Golden_frog_Kaieteur_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Anomaloglossus_beebei" title="Anomaloglossus beebei">Anomaloglossus beebei</a></i> (Kaieteur), specific to the Guianas
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rurrenabaque_Bolivia_-_The_Amazon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Rurrenabaque_Bolivia_-_The_Amazon.jpg/220px-Rurrenabaque_Bolivia_-_The_Amazon.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Rurrenabaque_Bolivia_-_The_Amazon.jpg/330px-Rurrenabaque_Bolivia_-_The_Amazon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Rurrenabaque_Bolivia_-_The_Amazon.jpg/440px-Rurrenabaque_Bolivia_-_The_Amazon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1607" data-file-height="1242"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rurrenabaque_Bolivia_-_The_Amazon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Hoatzin" title="Hoatzin">hoatzin</a> is the national bird of Guyana.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The following habitats have been categorised for Guyana: coastal, marine, littoral, estuarine palustrine, mangrove, riverine, lacustrine, swamp, savanna, white sand forest, brown sand forest, montane, cloud forest, moist lowland and dry evergreen scrub forests (NBAP, 1999). About 14 areas of biological interest have been identified as possible hotspots for a National Protected Area System. More than 80% of Guyana is still covered by forests, those forest also contains the world's rarest <a href="/wiki/Orchids" class="mw-redirect" title="Orchids">orchids</a> ranging from dry evergreen and seasonal forests to montane and lowland evergreen rain forests. These forests are home to more than a thousand species of trees. Guyana's tropical climate, unique geology, and relatively pristine ecosystems support extensive areas of species-rich rain forests and natural habitats with high levels of <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemism</a>. Approximately eight thousand species of plants occur in Guyana, half of which are found nowhere else. </p>
      <p>Guyana has one of the highest levels of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> in the world. With 1,168 <a href="/wiki/Vertebrate" title="Vertebrate">vertebrate</a> species and 814 bird species, it boasts one of the richest mammalian fauna assemblages of any comparably sized area in the world. Guyana is home to six ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Guayanan_Highlands_moist_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Guayanan Highlands moist forests">Guayanan Highlands moist forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guianan_moist_forests" title="Guianan moist forests">Guianan moist forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orinoco_Delta_swamp_forests" title="Orinoco Delta swamp forests">Orinoco Delta swamp forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tepuis" class="mw-redirect" title="Tepuis">Tepuis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guianan_savanna" title="Guianan savanna">Guianan savanna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guianan_mangroves" title="Guianan mangroves">Guianan mangroves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-34">[34]</a></sup> The Guiana Shield region is little known and extremely rich biologically. Unlike other areas of South America, over 70% of the natural habitat remains pristine. Guyana ranks third in the world with a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 9.58/10.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The rich natural history of British Guiana was described by early explorers Sir Walter Raleigh and Charles Waterton and later by naturalists Sir David Attenborough and Gerald Durrell. </p>
      <p>In February 2004, the Government of Guyana issued a title to more than 4,000 square kilometres (1<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup> acres) of land in the Konashen Indigenous District declaring this land as the Konashen Community-Owned Conservation Area (COCA), to be managed by the <a href="/wiki/Wai-Wai_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wai-Wai (people)">Wai Wai</a>. In doing so Guyana created the world's largest Community-Owned Conservation Area.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This important event followed a request made by the Wai Wai community to the government of Guyana and Conservation International Guyana (CIG) for assistance in developing a sustainable plan for their lands in Konashen. The three parties signed a Memorandum of Cooperation which outlines a plan for sustainable use of the Konashen COCA's biological resources, identifies threats to the area's biodiversity, and helps develop projects to increase awareness of the COCA as well as generate the income necessary to maintain its protected status. </p>
      <p>The Konashen Indigenous District of Southern Guyana houses the headwaters of the Essequibo River, Guyana's principal water source, and drains the Kassikaityu, Kamoa, Sipu and Chodikar rivers. Southern Guyana is host to some of the most pristine expanses of evergreen forests in the northern part of South America. Most of the forests found here are tall, evergreen hill-land and lower montane forests, with large expanses of flooded forest along major rivers. Thanks to the very low human population density of the area, most of these forests are still intact. The Smithsonian Institution has identified nearly 2,700 species of plants from this region, representing 239 distinct families, and there are certainly additional species still to be recorded. </p>
      <p>The diversity of plants supports diverse animal life, recently documented by a biological survey organised by Conservation International. The reportedly clean, unpolluted waters of the Essequibo watershed support a remarkable diversity of fish and aquatic invertebrates, and are home to <a href="/wiki/Giant_otters" class="mw-redirect" title="Giant otters">giant otters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capybaras" class="mw-redirect" title="Capybaras">capybaras</a>, and several species of <a href="/wiki/Caimans" class="mw-redirect" title="Caimans">caimans</a>. </p>
      <p>On land, large mammals, such as <a href="/wiki/Jaguar" title="Jaguar">jaguars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tapirs" class="mw-redirect" title="Tapirs">tapirs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bush_dog" title="Bush dog">bush dogs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giant_anteater" title="Giant anteater">giant anteaters</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saki_monkey" title="Saki monkey">saki monkeys</a> are still common. Over 400 species of birds have been reported from the region, and the reptile and amphibian faunas are similarly rich. The Konashen COCA forests are also home to countless species of insects, arachnids, and other invertebrates, many of which are still undiscovered or unnamed. </p>
      <p>The Konashen COCA contains a high level of biological diversity and richness that remains in nearly pristine condition; such places have become rare on earth. This fact has given rise to various non-exploitative, environmentally sustainable industries such as ecotourism, successfully capitalising on the biological wealth of the Konashen COCA with comparatively little enduring impact. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:20191121_Guyana_0048_Georgetown_sRGB_(49295795336).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/20191121_Guyana_0048_Georgetown_sRGB_%2849295795336%29.jpg/170px-20191121_Guyana_0048_Georgetown_sRGB_%2849295795336%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/20191121_Guyana_0048_Georgetown_sRGB_%2849295795336%29.jpg/255px-20191121_Guyana_0048_Georgetown_sRGB_%2849295795336%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/20191121_Guyana_0048_Georgetown_sRGB_%2849295795336%29.jpg/340px-20191121_Guyana_0048_Georgetown_sRGB_%2849295795336%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:20191121_Guyana_0048_Georgetown_sRGB_(49295795336).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Cathedral,_Georgetown" class="mw-redirect" title="St George's Cathedral, Georgetown">St George's Cathedral, Georgetown</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Cathedral,_Georgetown" title="St. George's Cathedral, Georgetown">St George's Anglican Cathedral</a>: A historic Anglican Cathedral made of wood.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Demerara_Harbour_Bridge" title="Demerara Harbour Bridge">Demerara Harbour Bridge</a>: The world's fourth-longest floating bridge.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Berbice_Bridge" title="Berbice Bridge">Berbice Bridge</a>: The world's sixth-longest floating bridge.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_the_Caribbean_Community" title="Secretariat of the Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community (CARICOM) Building</a>: Houses the headquarters of the largest and most powerful economic union in the Caribbean.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Providence_Stadium" title="Providence Stadium">Providence Stadium</a>: Situated on Providence on the north bank of the Demerara River and built in time for the ICC World Cup 2007, it is the largest sports stadium in the country. It is also near the Providence Mall, forming a major spot for leisure in Guyana.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Chung" title="Arthur Chung">Arthur Chung</a> Conference Centre:<sup id="cite_ref-Ministry_of_Public_Telecommunications_|_Republic_of_Guyana_2017_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ministry_of_Public_Telecommunications_|_Republic_of_Guyana_2017-37">[37]</a></sup> Presented as a gift from the People's Republic of China to the Government of Guyana. It is the only one of its kind in the country.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Stabroek_Market" title="Stabroek Market">Stabroek Market</a>: A large cast-iron colonial structure that looked like a statue was located next to the Demerara River.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Georgetown_City_Hall" title="Georgetown City Hall">City Hall</a>: A beautiful wooden structure also from the colonial era.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Takutu_River_Bridge" title="Takutu River Bridge">Takutu River Bridge</a>: A bridge across the Takutu River, connecting Lethem in Guyana to Bonfim in Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Umana_Yana" title="Umana Yana">Umana Yana</a>: An Amerindian benab, that is a national monument built in 1972, for a meeting of the Foreign Ministers of the Non-Aligned nations (It was rebuilt in 2016).</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Shell_Beach,_Guyana" title="Shell Beach, Guyana">Shell Beach</a>: Approximately 140&nbsp;km long beach. In some parts beach consists of pure shells, very high biological diversity. Important nesting site for 8 species of sea turtles.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Guyana" title="Economy of Guyana">Economy of Guyana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Guyana" title="Agriculture in Guyana">Agriculture in Guyana</a>
      </div>

      <div class="thumb tright">

        <a href="/wiki/File:Tractor_in_field_of_rice_by_Khirsah1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Tractor_in_field_of_rice_by_Khirsah1.jpg/220px-Tractor_in_field_of_rice_by_Khirsah1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Tractor_in_field_of_rice_by_Khirsah1.jpg/330px-Tractor_in_field_of_rice_by_Khirsah1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Tractor_in_field_of_rice_by_Khirsah1.jpg/440px-Tractor_in_field_of_rice_by_Khirsah1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Guyana_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Guyana_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/220px-Guyana_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Guyana_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/330px-Guyana_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Guyana_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/440px-Guyana_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="900"></a>

         </div>Graphical depiction of Guyana's product exports in 28 colour-coded categories (2017, very outdated, petroleum dominates the exports since year 2020)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The main economic activities in Guyana are agriculture (production of rice and <a href="/wiki/Natural_brown_sugar" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural brown sugar">Demerara sugar</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a> and gold mining, deep water Crude oil, timber, shrimp fishing and minerals. The sugar industry, which accounts for 28% of all export earnings, is largely run by the company <a href="/wiki/GuySuCo" class="mw-redirect" title="GuySuCo">GuySuCo</a>, which employs more people than any other industry. Many industries have a large foreign investment. For example, the American company <a href="/wiki/Reynolds_Metals" class="mw-redirect" title="Reynolds Metals">Reynolds Metals</a> and the British-Australian <a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Tinto Group">Rio Tinto's</a> Rio Tinto Alcan subsidiary are heavily invested in Guyana's mineral industry; the Korean/Malaysian Barama Company has a large stake in the logging industry. Since 2015, foreign companies have made several significant deep water <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_exploration_in_Guyana" class="mw-redirect" title="Petroleum exploration in Guyana">oil discoveries</a>. </p>
      <p>Chronic problems include a shortage of skilled <a href="/wiki/Labour_(economics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour (economics)">labour</a>, deficient infrastructure, and until recently, sizable external debt. Low prices for key mining and agricultural commodities, combined with troubles in the bauxite and sugar industries, had threatened the government's tenuous fiscal position and dimmed prospects for the future. However, the Guyanese economy has rebounded slightly and exhibited moderate economic growth since 1999, thanks to an expansion in the agricultural and mining sectors, a more favourable atmosphere for business initiatives, a more realistic exchange rate, fairly low inflation, and the continued support of international organisations. In 2008, the economy witnessed a 3% increase in growth amid the global <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">economic crisis</a>. It grew 5.4% in 2011 and 3.7% in 2012. According to IMF projections, economic growth is expected to be 53% in 2020 following the completion of the first off-shore oil project.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The production of <a href="/wiki/Balat%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Balatá">balatá</a> (natural <a href="/wiki/Latex" title="Latex">latex</a>) was once big business in Guyana. Most of the balata bleeding in Guyana took place in the foothills of the Kanuku Mountains in the Rupununi. Early exploitation also took place in the North West District, but most of the trees in the area were destroyed by illicit bleeding methods that involved cutting down the trees rather than making incisions in them. Uses of balatá included the making of <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> balls, the temporary filling of troublesome tooth cavities, and the crafting of figurines and other decorative items (particularly by the Macushi people of the Kanuku mountains). </p>
      <p>Major <a href="/wiki/Private_sector" title="Private sector">private sector</a> organisations include the Private Sector Commission (PSC)<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> and the Georgetown Chamber of Commerce &amp; Industry (GCCI);<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government initiated a major overhaul of the tax code in early 2007. A <a href="/wiki/Value_Added_Tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Value Added Tax">Value Added Tax</a> (VAT) replaced six different taxes. Prior to the implementation of the VAT, it had been relatively easy to evade sales tax, and many businesses were in violation of tax code. Many businesses opposed VAT introduction because of the extra paperwork required; however, the Government has remained firm on the VAT. By replacing several taxes with one flat tax rate, it will also be easier for government auditors to spot <a href="/wiki/Embezzlement" title="Embezzlement">embezzlement</a>. This was prevalent under the former PPP/C government who authorised the VAT to be equal to 50% of the value of the good.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>President Bharrat Jagdeo had made <a href="/wiki/Debt_relief" title="Debt relief">debt relief</a> a priority. He convinced the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">the World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank" title="Inter-American Development Bank">Inter-American Development Bank</a> (IDB) to write off US$800&nbsp;million of debt, and millions more owed to industrial nations. Jagdeo was lauded by IDB President Moreno for his strong leadership and negotiating skills.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary">Summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_and_regional_relations">International and regional relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: International and regional relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span id="The_Organisation_of_American_States_.28OAS.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Organisation_of_American_States_(OAS)">The <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_American_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation of American States">Organisation of American States</a> (OAS)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The Organisation of American States (OAS)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Guyana entered the Inter–American system in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Indigenous_Leaders_Summits_of_America_.28ILSA.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_Leaders_Summits_of_America_(ILSA)">Indigenous Leaders Summits of America (ILSA)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Indigenous Leaders Summits of America (ILSA)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>With Guyana having many groups of indigenous persons and given the geographical location of the country, the contributions of the Guyanese to the OAS respecting indigenous people may be significant.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The position of the OAS respecting indigenous persons developed over the years. "The "OAS has supported and participated in the organisation of Indigenous Leaders Summits of Americas (ILSA)"<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Draft American Declaration of the Rights of the Indigenous Persons appears to be a working document<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agreements_which_affect_financial_relationships">Agreements which affect financial relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Agreements which affect financial relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_.28CARICOM.29_Treaty_1994"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_(CARICOM)_Treaty_1994">The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>At a CARICOM Meeting, representatives of Trinidad and Tobago and Guyana respectively signed The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994 on 19 August 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This treaty covered taxes, residence, tax jurisdictions, capital gains, business profits, interest, dividends, royalties and other areas. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="FATCA">FATCA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: FATCA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>On 30 June 2014, Guyana signed a Model 1 agreement with the United States of America in relation to the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Account_Tax_Compliance_Act" title="Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act">Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act</a> (FATCA).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> This Model 1 agreement includes a reference to the Tax Information Exchange Agreement (Clause 3) which was signed on 22 July 1992 in Georgetown, Guyana intending to exchange Tax information on an automatic basis. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Guyana" title="Demographics of Guyana">Demographics of Guyana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guyanese_people" title="Guyanese people">Guyanese people</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Guyana_population_density.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Guyana_population_density.png/220px-Guyana_population_density.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="367" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Guyana_population_density.png/330px-Guyana_population_density.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Guyana_population_density.png/440px-Guyana_population_density.png 2x" data-file-width="452" data-file-height="753"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Guyana_population_density.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Guyana's population density in 2005 (people per km<sup>2</sup>)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Population_Guyana.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Population_Guyana.PNG/220px-Population_Guyana.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Population_Guyana.PNG/330px-Population_Guyana.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Population_Guyana.PNG/440px-Population_Guyana.PNG 2x" data-file-width="724" data-file-height="426"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Population_Guyana.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A graph showing the population of Guyana from 1961 to 2003. The population decline in the 1980s can be clearly seen.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The chief majority (about 90%) of Guyana's 773,000 population lives along a narrow coastal strip which ranges from a width of 16 to 64 kilometres (10 to 40&nbsp;mi) inland and which makes up approximately only 10% of the nation's total land area.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The present population of Guyana is racially and ethnically heterogeneous, with ethnic groups originating from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, as well as indigenous or aboriginal peoples. Despite their diverse ethnic backgrounds, these groups share two common languages: English and Creole. </p>
      <p>The largest ethnic group is the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Guyanese" title="Indo-Guyanese">Indo-Guyanese</a> (also known as <a href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbeans" title="Indo-Caribbeans">East Indians</a>), the descendants of indentured laborers from India, who make up 43.5% of the population, according to the 2002 census. They are followed by the <a href="/wiki/Afro-Guyanese" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Guyanese">Afro-Guyanese</a>, the descendants of slaves from Africa, who constitute 30.2%. The Guyanese of mixed heritage make up 16.7%, while the indigenous peoples (known locally as <a href="/wiki/Amerindians" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindians">Amerindians</a>) make up 9.1%. The indigenous groups include the <a href="/wiki/Lokono" title="Lokono">Arawaks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wai-wai_people" title="Wai-wai people">Wai Wai</a>, the Caribs, the <a href="/wiki/Akawaio_people" title="Akawaio people">Akawaio</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arecuna_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Arecuna people">Arecuna</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Patamona" class="mw-redirect" title="Patamona">Patamona</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wapixana" class="mw-redirect" title="Wapixana">Wapixana</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Macushi" title="Macushi">Macushi</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Warao_people" title="Warao people">Warao</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-43">[43]</a></sup> The two largest groups, the Indo-Guyanese and Afro-Guyanese, have experienced some racial tension.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most Indo-Guyanese are descended from indentured laborers who migrated from <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">North India</a>, especially the <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_region" title="Bhojpuri region">Bhojpur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Awadh" title="Awadh">Awadh</a> regions of the <a href="/wiki/Hindi_Belt" title="Hindi Belt">Hindi Belt</a> in the present day states of <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> A significant minority of Indo-Guyanese are also descended from indentured migrants who came from the South Indian states of <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">Andhra Pradesh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The distribution pattern in the 2002 census was similar to those of the 1980 and 1991 censuses, but the share of the two main groups has declined. Indo-Guyanese made up 51.9% of the total population in 1980, but by 1991 this had fallen to 48.6%, and then to 43.5% in the 2002 census. Those of African descent increased slightly from 30.8% to 32.3% during the first period (1980 and 1991) before falling to 30.2% in the 2002 census. With small growth in the overall population, the decline in the shares of the two larger groups has resulted in the relative increase of shares of the multiracial and Amerindian groups. The Amerindian population rose by 22,097 people between 1991 and 2002. This represents an increase of 47.3% or annual growth of 3.5%. Similarly, the multiracial population increased by 37,788 persons, representing a 43.0% increase or annual growth rate of 3.2% from the base period of 1991 census. </p>
      <p>The number of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guyanese" title="Portuguese Guyanese">Portuguese</a> people (4.3% of the population in 1891) has been declining constantly over the decades.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Guyana" title="Languages of Guyana">Languages of Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>English is the official language of Guyana and is used for education, government, media, and services. The vast majority of the population speaks <a href="/wiki/Guyanese_Creole" title="Guyanese Creole">Guyanese Creole</a>, an English-based creole with slight African, Indian, and Amerindian influence, as their native tongue.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In addition, the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Cariban_languages" title="Cariban languages">Cariban languages</a> (<a href="/wiki/Akawaio_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Akawaio language">Akawaio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waiwai_language" title="Waiwai language">Wai-Wai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Macushi_language" title="Macushi language">Macushi</a>) are spoken by a small minority of Amerindians. <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Hindustani#Guyanese_Hindustani" title="Caribbean Hindustani">Guyanese Hindustani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a> are retained and spoken by some Indo-Guyanese for cultural and religious reasons.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Guyana" title="Religion in Guyana">Religion in Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>According to a 2002 nationwide census on religious affiliation, 57.4% of the population was <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Guyana#Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianity in Guyana">Christian</a>, 28.4% was <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Guyana" title="Hinduism in Guyana">Hindu</a>, 7.2% was <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Guyana" title="Islam in Guyana">Muslim</a>, 1.9% adhered to other religions, while 2.3% of the population did not profess any.<sup id="cite_ref-CENSUS2002_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CENSUS2002-62">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Among Christians, most are Protestants (34.8%) or other Christian (20.8%), but there is also a minority of Roman Catholics (7.1%). Among Hindus, <a href="/wiki/San%C4%81tan%C4%AB" title="Sanātanī">Sanātanī</a> (orthodox Hinduism) is the major sect, along with a notable minority of those who follow the <a href="/wiki/Arya_Samaj_in_Guyana" title="Arya Samaj in Guyana">Arya Samaj</a>, and a smaller minority who follow the <a href="/wiki/International_Society_for_Krishna_Consciousness" title="International Society for Krishna Consciousness">ISKCON</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sathya_Sai_Baba_movement" title="Sathya Sai Baba movement">Sathya Sai Baba movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinmaya_Mission" title="Chinmaya Mission">Chinmaya Mission</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Kabir_Panth" class="mw-redirect" title="Kabir Panth">Kabir Panth</a>. Among Muslims, Sunni are in the majority, while there are also Shia and Ahmadiyya minorities. Among other religions, <a href="/wiki/Rastafarianism" class="mw-redirect" title="Rastafarianism">Rastafarianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith_in_Guyana" title="Baháʼí Faith in Guyana">Baha'i</a> faith are the most popular. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Guyana" title="Politics of Guyana">Politics of Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
