         </div>The Supreme Court of Guyana
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_building,_Guyana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Parliament_building%2C_Guyana.jpg/220px-Parliament_building%2C_Guyana.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Parliament_building%2C_Guyana.jpg/330px-Parliament_building%2C_Guyana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Parliament_building%2C_Guyana.jpg/440px-Parliament_building%2C_Guyana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="701" data-file-height="409"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_building,_Guyana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Guyana's parliament building since 1834
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Guyana" title="Politics of Guyana">politics of Guyana</a> takes place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, in which the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Guyana" title="President of Guyana">President of Guyana</a> is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and of a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the President and the Government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the President and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Guyana" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Guyana">National Assembly of Guyana</a>. Historically, politics are a source of tension in the country, and violent riots have often broken out during elections. During the 1970s and 1980s, the political landscape was dominated by the People's National Congress. </p>
      <p>In 1992, the first constitutional elections were overseen by former United States President <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>, and the People's Progressive Party led the country until 2015. The two parties are principally organised along ethnic lines and as a result often clash on issues related to the allocation of resources. In the General Elections held on 28 November 2011, the People's Progressive Party (PPP) retained a majority, and their presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Donald_Ramotar" title="Donald Ramotar">Donald Ramotar</a> was elected as president. </p>
      <p>On 11 May 2015, early general elections were held. A coalition of the A Partnership for National Unity-Alliance for Change (APNU-AFC) parties won 33 of the 65 seats in the National Assembly. On 16 May 2015, retired army general <a href="/wiki/David_A._Granger" title="David A. Granger">David A. Granger</a> became the eighth President of Guyana. However, on 21 December 2018, a vote of confidence was called for, regarding terms under which the government granted a franchise for offshore oil exploration. Legislator Charrandass Persaud defected from the coalition and the vote failed, requiring new elections. The governing coalition litigated this result for the entire 90 days allowed for new elections. New elections were held on March 02, 2020 and results were declared on August 03, 2020, with the People's Progressive Party/Civic as the winner. Dr. Irfaan Mohamed Ali became the ninth President of Guyana.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_procurement">Public procurement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Public procurement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Government_procurement" title="Government procurement">Public procurement</a> in Guyana is overseen by the Public Procurement Commission, appointed under the Public Procurement Commission Act 2003. Due to lengthy delay in identifying and agreeing commission members, the commission was not appointed until 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Guyana_Defence_Force" title="Guyana Defence Force">Guyana Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Guyana Defence Force (GDF) is the military service of Guyana. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Guyana" title="LGBT rights in Guyana">LGBT rights in Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">Homosexual</a> acts, as well as <a href="/wiki/Anal_sex" title="Anal sex">anal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oral_sex" title="Oral sex">oral sex</a> are illegal in Guyana.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> It is currently the only country in South America that prohibits such acts. Engaging in such acts can warrant <a href="/wiki/Life_imprisonment" title="Life imprisonment">life imprisonment</a>, though it is <a href="/wiki/Unenforced_law" title="Unenforced law">not enforced</a>. These laws can be difficult to alter, as <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Guyana" title="Constitution of Guyana">Guyana's Constitution</a> protects laws inherited from the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> from constitutional review.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Cross-dressing" title="Cross-dressing">cross-dressing</a> has been legal since 2018, when a ban was struck down by Guyana's court of last resort, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Court_of_Justice" title="Caribbean Court of Justice">Caribbean Court of Justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/President_of_Guyana" title="President of Guyana">President</a> <a href="/wiki/David_A._Granger" title="David A. Granger">David A. Granger</a> (2015–2020) expressed support for these efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure_and_telecommunications">Infrastructure and telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Infrastructure and telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Guyana" title="Transport in Guyana">Transport in Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:LethemBridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/LethemBridge.jpg/220px-LethemBridge.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/LethemBridge.jpg/330px-LethemBridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/LethemBridge.jpg/440px-LethemBridge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1050" data-file-height="713"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:LethemBridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cross-border bridge from Guyana to Brazil near <a href="/wiki/Lethem,_Guyana" title="Lethem, Guyana">Lethem</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are a total of 187 kilometres (116&nbsp;mi) of railway, all dedicated to ore transport. There are 7,969 kilometres (4,952&nbsp;mi) of highway, of which 591 kilometres (367&nbsp;mi) are paved. Navigable waterways extend 1,077 kilometres (669&nbsp;mi), including the Berbice, Demerara, and Essequibo rivers. There are ports at Georgetown, Port Kaituma, and <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam,_Guyana" title="New Amsterdam, Guyana">New Amsterdam</a>. There are two international airports (<a href="/wiki/Cheddi_Jagan_International_Airport" title="Cheddi Jagan International Airport">Cheddi Jagan International Airport</a>, Timehri and Eugene F. Correira International Airport (formerly <a href="/wiki/Ogle_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Ogle Airport">Ogle Airport</a>); along with about 90 airstrips, nine of which have paved runways. Guyana, Suriname and the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> are the only three regions in South America which <a href="/wiki/Drive_on_the_left" class="mw-redirect" title="Drive on the left">drive on the left</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity">Electricity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Electricity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electricity_sector_in_Guyana" title="Electricity sector in Guyana">Electricity sector in Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The electricity sector in Guyana is dominated by <a href="/wiki/Guyana_Power_and_Light" title="Guyana Power and Light">Guyana Power and Light</a> (GPL), the state-owned vertically integrated utility. Although the country has a large potential for hydroelectric and <a href="/wiki/Bagasse" title="Bagasse">bagasse</a>-fueled power generation, most of its 226 <a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">MW</a> of installed capacity correspond to diesel-engine driven generators.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Several initiatives are in place to improve <a href="/wiki/Hinterland_energy_in_Guyana" title="Hinterland energy in Guyana">energy access in the hinterland</a>. Guyana is endowed with renewable energy resources and is likely to benefit greatly from the energy transition. It is ranked no. 3 among 156 countries in the index of geopolitical gains and losses after energy transition (GeGaLo Index).<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Guyana" title="Health in Guyana">Health in Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth is estimated to be 67.39 years for both males and females in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> The PAHO/ WHO Global Health Report 2014 (using statistics of 2012) ranked the country as having the highest <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">suicide</a> rate in the world, with a mortality rate of 44.2 per 100,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> According to 2011 estimates from the <a href="/wiki/WHO" class="mw-redirect" title="WHO">WHO</a>, <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> <a href="/wiki/Prevalence" title="Prevalence">prevalence</a> is 1.2% of the teen/adult population (ages 15–49).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Guyana" title="Education in Guyana">Education in Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Queens_College_Guyana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Queens College Guyana.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Queens_College_Guyana.jpg/220px-Queens_College_Guyana.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Queens_College_Guyana.jpg/330px-Queens_College_Guyana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Queens_College_Guyana.jpg/440px-Queens_College_Guyana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="686" data-file-height="521"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Queens_College_Guyana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>

         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">

          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Guyana lacks a critical mass of expertise in many of the disciplines and activities on which it depends. At 88.5%, Guyana's <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_literacy_rate" title="List of countries by literacy rate">lowest</a> in South America.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Guyanese education system is modelled on the former <a href="/wiki/British_education" class="mw-redirect" title="British education">British education</a> system. Students are expected to take the NGSA (National Grade Six Assessment) for entrance into high school in grade 7. They take the <a href="/wiki/CXC" class="mw-redirect" title="CXC">CXC</a> at the end of high school. Schools have introduced the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Advanced_Proficiency_Examination" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Advanced Proficiency Examination">CAPE</a> exams which all other Caribbean countries have introduced. The <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Level_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced Level (UK)">A-level system</a>, inherited from the British era, is offered only in a few schools. </p>
      <p>President of Guyana Dr Irfaan Ali on the new year of 2021 made a major announcement for public sector employees mostly related to education sector. He announced a one-off cash grant of $25,000 each to workers of the whole Public Sector, including those who are currently employed at GuySuco.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Guyana" title="Culture of Guyana">Culture of Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Guyana" class="mw-redirect" title="Literature of Guyana">Literature of Guyana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Guyana" title="Music of Guyana">Music of Guyana</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">

      <p>Guyana's culture is very similar to that of the English-speaking Caribbean, and has historically been tied to the English-speaking Caribbean as part of the British Empire when it became a possession in the nineteenth century. Guyana is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Caricom" class="mw-redirect" title="Caricom">Caricom</a> (Caribbean Community) economic bloc and also the home of the Bloc's Headquarters, the CARICOM Secretariat. </p>
      <p>Guyana's geographical location, its sparsely populated rain-forest regions, and its substantial Amerindian population differentiate it from English-speaking Caribbean countries. Its blend of Indo-Guyanese (East Indian) and Afro-Guyanese (African) cultures gives it similarities to <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> and distinguishes it from other parts of the Americas. Guyana shares similar interests with the islands in the West Indies, such as food, festive events, music, sports, etc. </p>
      <p>Guyana plays international cricket as a part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="West Indian cricket team">West Indies cricket team</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Guyanese_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Guyanese cricket team">Guyana team</a> plays <a href="/wiki/First_class_cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="First class cricket">first-class cricket</a> against other nations of the Caribbean. In March and April 2007 Guyana co-hosted the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="Cricket World Cup 2007">Cricket World Cup 2007</a>. In addition to its CARICOM membership, Guyana is a member of <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a>, the international football federation for North and Central America and the Caribbean. </p>
      <p>Events include <a href="/wiki/Mashramani" title="Mashramani">Mashramani</a> (Mash), <a href="/wiki/Phagwah" class="mw-redirect" title="Phagwah">Phagwah</a> (<a href="/wiki/Holi" title="Holi">Holi</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Deepavali" class="mw-redirect" title="Deepavali">Deepavali</a> (<a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">Diwali</a>). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Guyana is home to more than 900 species of birds; 225 species of mammals; 880 species of reptiles and more than 6,500 different species of plants.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> Among these wildlife categories the most notably famous are the <a href="/wiki/Arapaima" title="Arapaima">Arapaima</a>, which is the world's largest scaled freshwater fish, <a href="/wiki/Giant_anteater" title="Giant anteater">giant anteater</a>, the largest anteater, <a href="/wiki/Giant_otter" title="Giant otter">giant otter</a>, the world's largest and rarest river otter and lastly the most notably famous of birds, cock of the rock (<i><a href="/wiki/Rupicola_rupicola" class="mw-redirect" title="Rupicola rupicola">Rupicola rupicola</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Providence_Stadium_outside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Providence_Stadium_outside.jpg/220px-Providence_Stadium_outside.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Providence_Stadium_outside.jpg/330px-Providence_Stadium_outside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Providence_Stadium_outside.jpg/440px-Providence_Stadium_outside.jpg 2x" data-file-width="931" data-file-height="516"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Providence_Stadium_outside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Providence Stadium as seen from the East Bank Highway
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The major sports in Guyana are <a href="/wiki/Guyana_national_cricket_team" title="Guyana national cricket team">cricket</a> (Guyana is part of the West Indies as defined for international cricket purposes<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Basketball_in_Guyana" title="Basketball in Guyana">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, and volleyball.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> Minor sports include <a href="/wiki/Beach_cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="Beach cricket">softball cricket (beach cricket)</a>, field hockey, <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rounders" title="Rounders">rounders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lawn_tennis" class="mw-redirect" title="Lawn tennis">lawn tennis</a>, table tennis, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squash_(sport)" title="Squash (sport)">squash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana_national_rugby_union_team" title="Guyana national rugby union team">rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a> and a few others. </p>
      <p>Guyana played host to <a href="/wiki/International_cricket" title="International cricket">international cricket</a> matches as part of the <a href="/wiki/2007_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2007 Cricket World Cup">2007 Cricket World Cup</a> (CWC 2007). The new 15,000-seat <a href="/wiki/Providence_Stadium" title="Providence Stadium">Providence Stadium</a>, also referred to as Guyana National Stadium, was built in time for the World Cup and was ready for the beginning of play on 28 March. At the first international game of CWC 2007 at the stadium, <a href="/wiki/Lasith_Malinga" title="Lasith Malinga">Lasith Malinga</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_national_cricket_team" title="Sri Lanka national cricket team">Sri Lankan team</a> took four wickets in four consecutive deliveries.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Guyana%27s_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Guyana's national basketball team">Guyana's national basketball team</a> has traditionally been one of the top contenders at the <a href="/wiki/CaribeBasket" class="mw-redirect" title="CaribeBasket">CaribeBasket</a>, the top international basketball tournament for countries in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. </p>
      <p>For international football purposes, <a href="/wiki/Guyana_national_football_team" title="Guyana national football team">Guyana</a> is part of CONCACAF. The highest league in their club system is the <a href="/wiki/GFF_Elite_League" title="GFF Elite League">GFF Elite League</a>. <a href="/wiki/Guyana_national_football_team" title="Guyana national football team">Guyana's national football team</a> has never qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>, however they qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Cup" title="Caribbean Cup">Caribbean Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1991_Caribbean_Cup" title="1991 Caribbean Cup">1991</a>, finishing fourth, and <a href="/wiki/2007_Caribbean_Cup" title="2007 Caribbean Cup">2007</a>. In 2019, they qualified for the <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Gold_Cup" title="CONCACAF Gold Cup">CONCACAF Gold Cup</a> for the first time, after finishing 7th in the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_CONCACAF_Nations_League_qualifying" title="2019–20 CONCACAF Nations League qualifying">qualifiers</a>. They finished 3rd in Group D, having lost two matches and drawn one. </p>
      <p>Guyana also has five courses for horse racing.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guyana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-61">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mostly made up of other <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a>, but also <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mormons" title="Mormons">Mormons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> and other Christians.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
